  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_019affcd-9be7-4562-a88c-d130f1701a6c'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_2177744110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177744110" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177744110?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=literally-painful-to-read">literally-painful-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177744110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer705465159571372119"><b>Why, why, whyyyyyy do I keep torturing myself with these novels?</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Deeeeeeep Breaths</i>
</b><br/><br/>This book <b>
  <u>added nothing of value</u>
</b> to the entire series. Why? Cause we're able to piece together the entire plot from blatantly obvious foreshadowing (or would that be back-shadowing?) from the original trilogy. <br/><br/>Secret Government Agency to get rid of virus? <b>Yup, figured that one out in the first book.</b> <br/><br/>Maze is designed by children? <b>Hinted at and later confirmed in book 2.</b> <br/><br/>And on....and on.........and on........</span>
  <span id="freeText705465159571372119" style="display:none"><b>Why, why, whyyyyyy do I keep torturing myself with these novels?</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Deeeeeeep Breaths</i>
</b><br /><br />This book <b>
  <u>added nothing of value</u>
</b> to the entire series. Why? Cause we're able to piece together the entire plot from blatantly obvious foreshadowing (or would that be back-shadowing?) from the original trilogy. <br /><br />Secret Government Agency to get rid of virus? <b>Yup, figured that one out in the first book.</b> <br /><br />Maze is designed by children? <b>Hinted at and later confirmed in book 2.</b> <br /><br />And on....and on.........and on.............(you get the point). <br /><br /><u>
  <b>AND WE STILL DON'T GET THE IMPORTANT ANSWER</b>
</u><br /><br /><b><u>WHY</u> is there a freaking <u>MAZE</u></b> used to solve a viral zombie infection? <br /><br />How in the world does that even make the least bit sense? Sure, they sprout off some mumbo-jumbo about brain patterns due to decision-making skills but<b> even I can smell that bull.</b> <br /><br />MAYBE the scientists could take the millions of dollars they spent on creating movable 40-foot walls, spider-slug-robot hybrids, and insanely specific mind-wiping drugs...and INVEST it in something else - <b>
  <u>LIKE ACTUAL RESEARCH.</u>
</b><br /><br />I did (semi) enjoy reading about the childhood of the Maze Runner characters. It was a bit interesting to see how deeply WICKED manipulated their lives but even that fell short - mostly cause Thomas had (still has) as much <b>personality as a pancake</b> and Theresa was (and still is) a <b>back-stabbing wench.</b><br /><br /><b>Wasn't a fan before, <i>definitely</i> not now</b><br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />As far as audiobooks go, it's not a bad one. But the plot just soured everything for me.<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_1119244181" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1119244181" />
    <a title="Kelly Brigid ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24407332-kelly-brigid"><img alt="Kelly Brigid ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557200443p2/24407332.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1119244181?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Brigid ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Brigid ♡" href="/user/show/24407332-kelly-brigid">Kelly Brigid ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24407332-kelly-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1119244181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11906151442396941709">0.5) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978318' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Kill Order</a> ★✰✰✰✰<br/>1) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978243' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Maze Runner</a> ★★★✰✰<br/>2) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978256' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Scorch Trials</a> ★★✰✰✰<br/>3) <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978275' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Death Cure</a> ★✰✰✰✰<br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You look bloody fantastic for three in the morning.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><i>“WICKED was never going to stop. They were never, never going to stop.”</i><b> Apparently, neither was Dashner.</b> I have a strange attachment to this series, despite disliking most aspects of it. The Maze Runner was one of the first young adult series I read, so it’s a shame I have such negative opinions towards it now. The story itself is intr</span>
  <span id="freeText11906151442396941709" style="display:none">0.5) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978318" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kill Order</a> ★✰✰✰✰<br>1) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978243" rel="nofollow noopener">The Maze Runner</a> ★★★✰✰<br>2) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978256" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorch Trials</a> ★★✰✰✰<br>3) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754978275" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death Cure</a> ★✰✰✰✰<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“You look bloody fantastic for three in the morning.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><i>“WICKED was never going to stop. They were never, never going to stop.”</i><b> Apparently, neither was Dashner.</b> I have a strange attachment to this series, despite disliking most aspects of it. The Maze Runner was one of the first young adult series I read, so it’s a shame I have such negative opinions towards it now. The story itself is intriguing, but I loathe the writing, and couldn’t look past all the the plot holes. The sole reason I read The Fever Code was so I could receive answers to the many questions the trilogy left me with. This prequel unfortunately, didn’t clear up any questions about the plot, and added nothing significant to the series. Nearly all the information presented was already known, and there was only one element that was partially eye-opening. I was also expecting this book to be written in different point-of-view’s, so I was gravely upset when ninety-nine percent of it was in Thomas’ perspective – who still has about as much personality as an animal documentary narrator. <br><br><b>One of my biggest complaints is Dashner’s writing.</b> I was truly hoping that his writing would have improved, but I was disappointed. It’s as monotonous as I remembered it being in The Maze Runner. I also found it exhausting to read from Thomas’ perspective. He has no distinct personality, and isn’t nearly as intelligent as he is suggested to be. His ignorance is incredibly frustrating, especially considering that the reader is already aware of WICKED’s intentions. Which brings me to my next issue …<br><br><b>Nothing new or relevant is uncovered in this backstory.</b> I was expecting answers to questions such as, why are the trials necessary? How exactly do these variables lead to a cure? Why is the government wasting all its resources on constructing mazes and having children complete puzzles, when they can be doing something relevant with their time and money? Why not try virtual reality? This worked in Dashner’s other series! The approaches taken to find a cure are foolish, and I find it difficult to believe that the decisions that were made, came from intelligent scientists. With all the advance technologies and knowledge at their disposal, a maze filled with robotic slugs was their best solution? Why not try meaningful research?<br><br><b>This novel was approximately 350 pages, and bore me to sleep.</b> Perhaps I’m being a bit harsh, but I simply wasn’t invested in the plot. The vast majority of the story revolves around Thomas’ dull classes that I didn’t care for. It’s quite repetitive, and wasn’t very intriguing. Although the last quarter of this novel picks up and we’re presented with some action, it unfortunately didn’t entice me, since I already lost nearly all interest in the plot, 200 pages prior the finale.<br><br>A small revelation occurred in this novel that was never expressed in the other Maze Runner books – <b>the Grievers’ stingers contain mutated variants of the Flare virus … and WICKED has an antidote for this.</b> By that logic, shouldn’t the scientists have found a way to develop a stronger serum based from that antidote? An antidote that could maybe cure the whole world and make it irrelevant to create a maze? Why didn’t WICKED invest all their efforts in that instead? Oh, how this series drives me insane.<br><br><b>In spite of the dozens of problems I had with this book, there are a few aspects I enjoyed.</b> I promise you I’m not a heartless critic! I loved how we were able to see my little Gladers once more! I truly missed Newt, Minho, and Chuck! I was willing to forgive how absurd it was that practically every character from the series makes an appearance in this prequel, because I adore these characters so much. I was hoping to read a decent amount of this book from Newt’s point-of-view, but although this didn’t happen, I was still glad to read his prologue. I was also pleased to of had more insight on the Purge and what Thomas and Teresa’s roles were in it. The details regarding this momentous event, as well as the background of WICKED, were obscure in the original trilogy, so it was nice how more information was provided.<br><br><b>I don’t know what to think about The Maze Runner books any more.</b> At a glance, the series is quite mediocre and doesn’t have a compelling plot, nor unique characters. Yet, I still find myself being entertained by the story. Would I recommend this series? No. The plot holes are too immense to look past, the writing is too simple, and the protagonist isn’t very agreeable. However, if you ever do decide to read these books, I wouldn’t suggest reading The Fever Code first, because it does display many elements that are a mystery for most of the novels.<br><br><a href="https://justanotherbookinthewall.wordpress.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/anotherbookinthewall/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/kelly_reads" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/another-book-in-wall-18441447" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin</a><br><br>--------------------------------<br><br><b>
  <u>November 30, 2014</u>
</b><br><br>Oh shuck it, the cover and synopsis have been revealed! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491836272i/22452977._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11906151442396941709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText6020137590574115436" style="display:none">Um. I sat here forever trying to figure out what I want the stars to be. I will just go with the three star rating. <br /><br />I LOVED reading about the group again and reading about how some of them were taken and their ages. Those WICKED people really are evil. I'm guessing they picked the right name. <br /><br />I just can't believe the kids lived all of their years there and just ugh. <br /><br />And that creepy guy coming down the hall, "Save Me, Save me" Well, I don't remember if that's exactly what he said but along those lines. <br /><br />That ending! I mean we all know what happens, at least the ones that have read the Maze Runner books but that was just cold. But, I still liked to see where it all came from, the before of where they were when they landed in the maze. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6020137590574115436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15442947420668905984"><i> "And now he needed to say something smart, something profound, something that would bind them together and start the terrible journey."<br/>"This sucks" </i><br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed this Maze Runner prequel! We get insight into Thomas and Teresa's lives as they grow up within WICKED and all the brain washing that comes with it . We get to meet all the characters from the original trilogy - all before they enter the maze.<br/>It was really interesting to view things from this perspective, to watch the build up to</span>
  <span id="freeText15442947420668905984" style="display:none"><i> "And now he needed to say something smart, something profound, something that would bind them together and start the terrible journey."<br />"This sucks" </i><br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed this Maze Runner prequel! We get insight into Thomas and Teresa's lives as they grow up within WICKED and all the brain washing that comes with it . We get to meet all the characters from the original trilogy - all before they enter the maze.<br />It was really interesting to view things from this perspective, to watch the build up to the maze trials and to see how involved Thomas and Teresa were and how their mindsets changed over time.<br />With all the action and drama we've come to expect from the maze runner books, this was a welcome addition and it has made me want to go back and reread all the trilogy again!</span>

<div id="review_1305373073" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305373073" />
    <a title="Vivianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012562-vivianne"><img alt="Vivianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580677327p2/33012562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1305373073?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivianne" href="/user/show/33012562-vivianne">Vivianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012562-vivianne?shelf=a-owned">a-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012562-vivianne?shelf=z-3-stars">z-3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012562-vivianne?shelf=unhaul-shelve">unhaul-shelve</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1305373073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10992272630137506485"><b>This book was definitely the missing piece in this series, but I was left with more questions after reading this then going in. This book lacked the tension and twists the previous books had and it had some boring and weird chapters. It wasn’t renewing enough for a book that was supposed to have all the answered. I’m really disappointed. The three stars are for Thomas and the other Gladers, the prologue, for the amazing writing style James has and for the few answers I did get.</b> <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1005826028?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1%20' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Kill Order: 5</a></span>
  <span id="freeText10992272630137506485" style="display:none"><b>This book was definitely the missing piece in this series, but I was left with more questions after reading this then going in. This book lacked the tension and twists the previous books had and it had some boring and weird chapters. It wasn’t renewing enough for a book that was supposed to have all the answered. I’m really disappointed. The three stars are for Thomas and the other Gladers, the prologue, for the amazing writing style James has and for the few answers I did get.</b> <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1005826028?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1%20" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kill Order: 5 stars </a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305373073?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1%20" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fever Code: 3 stars</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1005825539?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1%20" rel="nofollow noopener">The Maze Runner: 5+ stars!</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1005825628?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1%20" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scorch Trials: 5 stars</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1005825662?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Death Cure: 4 stars</a><br><br>The maze runner trilogy is one of my favorite series of all time. But if I must be honest, <b>it was sometimes like a weird dream.</b> Not that I didn’t like that, but like in a dream there are not much logical explanations and that was a really big flaw of this series. After finishing the books in the trilogy I was left with a lot of <b>WHY?</b> <i>Why was the maze necessary for finding a cure? Why where there two teams? Why only boys and the other only girls? Why throw Thomas and Teresa in last? Why where they even special? Why would this help cure the disease? (I have a lot more but I will stop now)</i> So I was so happy to find out that this book was produced and that the synopsis was: <b>The story of how the maze was built.</b> Unfortunately none of my questions got answered. I also still feel like that this series has a wrong order, I mean isn’t it weird that we already know the ending and what will happen? It took away so much of the tension in this book.<br><br><br><b>CONTAINS SOME MINOR SPOILERS FROM DOWN HERE. Major spoilers if you haven’t read the other books in “The Maze Runner” series!!!! </b><br><br><blockquote>
<i>”Stephen, Stephen, Stephen. My name is Stephen. </i><br>He figured he had two things to hold on to: his memories and his name. Surely they couldn’t take the first away from him, but they were trying to steal the second. For two days they’d pressed him to accept his new name: Thomas.”</blockquote><br><br>This book had me crying, JEP CRYING, the first 6 pages. I’ve always loved Newt in the Maze Runner and this epilogue was emotional and heartbreaking. <br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>The first 200 pages where almost boring (with the exception of the prologue). They weren’t exciting, full of action and tense like the other books where. I was actually disappointed while reading. This book wasn’t as I had expected The Fever Code to be. I thought it would maybe contain short stories from all the Gladers about how they came with WICKED and how they then came in the maze. For some reason I didn’t expected Thomas to be the main character of this whole book. It just described how he lived with WICKED and that he builds the maze, didn’t we already know this? I got so tired of reading that Thomas was feeling alone and that he hated WICKED. Not that I didn’t feel sorry for him but <b>I didn’t care reading about almost every class he took and how many tests he had to take.</b> I wanted some Newt and Minho inside!!!! I was also annoyed that Thomas is kept in the dark so much, I understand from WICKED’s point of view but as a reader I was so annoyed! The first 200 pages aren’t renewing enough for a book that was supposed to have all the answered. I did like to read about what happened in the maze before Thomas and Teresa came in. Though I found the chapters about this way to short, I would have liked some more! <br><blockquote>”But why do they keep us separate?” Newt asked, and the sadness in his voice broke Thomas’s heart. “Why all the tests and the games and the cruelty? I hate them.”</blockquote><br><br>Besides Thomas’s daily classes and tests there were also some scenes about Thomas building friendships with the Gladers. <b>I enjoyed reading about Thomas building the friendships</b> and how cute and innocent they were as little children. But I don’t understand the purpose of letting them run in the hallways when they weren’t allowed? Was that also a test? I just don’t understand!? But I liked reading about Thomas, Teresa and the others as children. Five year old Thomas and Teresa, cuteeeee.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491901971ra/22458938.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I once again loved Thomas! He’s a great main character. </b><br>Unfortunately I never really liked Teresa. I never understood her in the previous books, I always thought she was distant and maybe even a bit haughtily. She did some things that I wasn’t a fan of. But she redeemed herself in the first part of this book. She’s very smart, curious and badass. I loved her and Thomas their friendship in this book! But from page 200 <b>she got all annoying again,</b> keeping things from Thomas and believing everything WICKED said. And then she sold Thomas out, and I went back to hating her again. I also intensely hate dr. Paige!! I hated how she never answered Thomas, was just trying to smooth talk things like killing 19 people, how she manipulated everything, how she used every single person as a test subject and for what becomes clear in the end.<br>I loved Chucks role in this book. I always wanted to know more from the kid and he’s so cute and funny. <b>All the other Gladers and the characters from group A had a relative small part,</b> which I was kind of angry about. This book was supposed to give us more inside on them but I didn’t really got that. I only liked the few parts about Newt. <br><br>After the boring 200 pages The Purge happened.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The Flare has gotten into wicked and infected some of the staff. Thomas, Teresa, Aris and Rachel are given the assignment to go and kill all the infected. WHAT THE HELL?! I thought they were supposed to be The Special Elite? They can’t even go outside without 2 guards and now you are going to let them kill Cranks because they are immune? No logic to this at all! I think Dashner is trying to create some suspense which he succeeded in but I HATED how! The reason why they got sick was a nice twist though. Made me remember why I hate dr. Paige again. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>I missed Dashner’s writing style so much. I don’t know why but it just appeals to me.</b> No unnecessary details but still enough to not make it boring and still have an interesting world building. It lets some to my imagination! It’s also really fluent and I liked the short chapters. I will definitely read more from him in the future. I do, however, have to comment on how James described the disease and how WICKED is trying to find a cure. This is absolute bullshit, it could never happen like this. But I also kind of liked how he created this totally unrealistic Kill zone. <br><br>I thought this book was supposed to explain to us the quote: WICKED is good? But all I read about was child abuse, imprisoning, and physical and mental abuse. WICKED IS <b>NOT</b> GOOD!!! Even if the whole world is dead you can’t do this to the only people that are the only ones that stand a chance to survive, the Munies. I don’t get that WICKED can be this cruel to children.<br><br><b> Things I got wiser: (SPOILERS don’t click if you don’t want to know the plot!)</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[1: Sonja is Newt’s sister Liss.<br>2: WICKED is even more full of shit than I thought.<br>3: The Flare was made by man who thought the world population got too big. But the disease got out of hand.<br><blockquote>”He would always remember that WICKED was trying to fix a problem their predecessors had created in the first place.”</blockquote>
<br>4: Grievers carried a mutated form of the disease that also the immune could get, the syringes contained the antidote. (Don’t understand this because then they would have an antidote for the flare, right?)<br>5: Chancellor Paige and Teresa are terrible traitors.<br>6: Teresa didn’t get her memories wiped before going into the maze.<br>7: Conformation that Deedee is infect Theresa.<br>8: What happened to Newt’s legs. <br>9: That Thomas is not on WICKED’s side and is trying to save his friends.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><blockquote>”You were always my favorite, Thomas.” Dr. Paige said. “Let’s get him prepped.”</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10992272630137506485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1704937158" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064855707?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricky" href="/user/show/7644190-ricky">Ricky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=freaky-supernatural-adventures">freaky-supernatural-adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=action-adventures">action-adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=apocalyptic-or-post-apocalyptic">apocalyptic-or-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=read-this-if-it-kills-you">read-this-if-it-kills-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7644190-ricky?shelf=why-isn-t-this-a-bloody-movie-yet">why-isn-t-this-a-bloody-movie-yet</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064855707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9606372214959053507">"<i>They march on through the dust<br/>Believe their leader, they can trust<br/>In all the noise they lose the way...</i><br/>-Kongos <br/><br/>Well. This is it. The <i>Maze Runner</i> prequel we've all been waiting for.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411585047ra/11252201.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I should warn you, though...it wouldn't be a Dashner book without a few moments that make you go all...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406047134ra/10493897.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399491461ra/9559225.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476586105ra/20859653.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The original trilogy, those helped define the end of my time in high school and the start of my community college years (<i>Death Cure</i> having come out about a month after I started there.) Then came <i>The Kill Order</i>, whic</span>
  <span id="freeText9606372214959053507" style="display:none">"<i>They march on through the dust<br>Believe their leader, they can trust<br>In all the noise they lose the way...</i><br>-Kongos <br><br>Well. This is it. The <i>Maze Runner</i> prequel we've all been waiting for.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411585047ra/11252201.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I should warn you, though...it wouldn't be a Dashner book without a few moments that make you go all...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406047134ra/10493897.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399491461ra/9559225.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476586105ra/20859653.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The original trilogy, those helped define the end of my time in high school and the start of my community college years (<i>Death Cure</i> having come out about a month after I started there.) Then came <i>The Kill Order</i>, which I loved when I first read it, but alone of the <i>Maze Runner</i> books, it's probably the only one I wouldn't re-read.<br><br>When news broke that there would be a new prequel focusing on the Gladers we know and love, well, you can imagine I was just as overjoyed as anyone else in the fandom.<br><br>After taking a few years to write <i>The Mortality Doctrine</i>, Dashner's finally given us <i>The Fever Code</i> in all its post-apocalyptic glory. Imagine, if you will, <i>Ender's Game</i> with zombie Cranks instead of alien Formics. That's the roughest, most high-concept summary of this book I could come up with. The primary difference, though, is that in between all the laughs and fun of Thomas, Teresa, Alby, Minho, Newt, Chuck, and more meeting up before the Maze, there's a ton of horror both physical and psychological. Physical because we're seeing the monsters as visceral as ever (especially after seeing the first two very stellar movies, with their creepy clicking Grievers and Cranks crawling all up and down the bloody walls!), and psychological because we all know what's coming if we've read the original trilogy first - and yet, we don't. Some of those WICKED people are every bit as wicked as you can imagine. Not gonna name any Randall names, but...some of those shucking klunk piles needed Launcher shots to the chest.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442821764ra/16282502.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If Wes Ball doesn't get a chance to direct the <i>Fever Code</i> movie, this world's getting cheated.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442821764ra/16282505.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now that we have another year to wait until the <i>Death Cure</i> movie, at least we've got this book to tide us over. And what a book that is, one of the most intense, raw YA books of 2016 so far...and now topping my list of favorite books of the year. For sure, just like the <i>Scorch Trials</i> movie won a Pinecone Award last year, this book's full-tilt, panic-inducing story guarantees it a win this year.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476586105ra/20859654.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, once again, a huge thank you to James Dashner for penning these books, helping set the stage for Dylan O'Brien to become this generation's next great action hero, teaching us all that "WICKED is good," and of course for just plain horror-fying YA literature like nobody else.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476586105ra/20859655.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9606372214959053507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1566994961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566994961" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566994961?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781910655160" href="/book/show/30627589-the-fever-code">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=science-fiction-sagacity">science-fiction-sagacity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566994961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1599068333822676787"><b>First Read: September 2017, Rating: 4 Stars<br/>Second Read: October 2018, Rating: 4 Stars</b><br/><br/>For an ardent dystopian fan such as myself, ‘The Maze Runner’ series is the gift that keeps on giving. Not only are there three books in the original trilogy, but two full-length prequel novels.<br/><br/>This takes place directly before the events that occur in The Maze Runner, yet should be read last, as per Dashner’s specific instructions. The book chronicles the conception of the WICKED organisation, as well as how Tho</span>
  <span id="freeText1599068333822676787" style="display:none"><b>First Read: September 2017, Rating: 4 Stars<br />Second Read: October 2018, Rating: 4 Stars</b><br /><br />For an ardent dystopian fan such as myself, ‘The Maze Runner’ series is the gift that keeps on giving. Not only are there three books in the original trilogy, but two full-length prequel novels.<br /><br />This takes place directly before the events that occur in The Maze Runner, yet should be read last, as per Dashner’s specific instructions. The book chronicles the conception of the WICKED organisation, as well as how Thomas, Teresa, Newt, and the rest of the beloved gang, came to be affiliated with it.<br /><br />As in the other books, the reader is invited into this near future vision of our world through the eyes of Thomas. His astute observations give us an honest insight into events but his young age, and the plethora of information that his kept for him means the truth of the situations are unfurled slowly for both the reader and himself.<br /><br />With the suspense at an all-time high, and the reader already aware of the traumatic events that are to follow, this is possibly the most poignant and emotional franchise instalment. The young cast of characters are depicted as innocent bystanders helplessly caught up in an organisation that has no regard for them as humans. The moment they stepped through the compound doors, however unwillingly, they became WICKED test subjects and nothing more. Whilst this fact has always been known, The Fever Code confronts the reader with the reality of this utterly heartbreaking scenario and disallows any of our sorrow to be spared.<br /><br />Despite the brutality of the organisation and the loneliness and confusion experienced by the children imprisoned there, this isn’t a book without its joyous moments. And knowing how hard each smile was fought for made every fleeting moment of happiness that much more precious for both reader and characters alike.<br /><br />By this alignment of emotion, it meant that as the novel progressed, the action increased, and the suspense rose in intensity, the reader was already placed firmly on one of the two opposing sides. With differing opinions on what was deemed an acceptable action to save the world, this also posed a multitude of philosophical questions that added some levity to the previous action-dominated plot-lines of this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1599068333822676787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9740326885117801240"><b> WICKED was never going to stop. They were never never going to stop </b><br/><br/>i feel like this book was the missing piece in this story but it still left me with so many questions that i need answered. I've been waiting for another prequel like this that answered my questions from the trilogy and i wasn't disappointed of course. <br/><br/>I loved the multiple POV's in the book from all of my favourite characters especially Minho and Chuck and i was happy to also see all the other characters from the trilogy come b</span>
  <span id="freeText9740326885117801240" style="display:none"><b> WICKED was never going to stop. They were never never going to stop </b><br /><br />i feel like this book was the missing piece in this story but it still left me with so many questions that i need answered. I've been waiting for another prequel like this that answered my questions from the trilogy and i wasn't disappointed of course. <br /><br />I loved the multiple POV's in the book from all of my favourite characters especially Minho and Chuck and i was happy to also see all the other characters from the trilogy come back in this prequel. Thomas was one of the POV in the story and i finally learned what he was like in the early years before the Maze and during the beginning of the Maze been created by him and three other kids with the help from WICKED. I started to like Thomas more in this one and this book restored that like after i didn't like him in the third book of the trilogy. Teresa was also in this book and i honestly still have a strong dislike for this character and this book just makes this dislike stronger, theres just something about her that i can't seem to ever like about her. She was a liar throughout the whole book once again like she was in the trilogy keeping secrets and lying to Thomas but i know she had her own agenda that she was trying to live up to. <br /><br />It was really enjoyable reading from Newts POV in the book because you got an insight to what his character is like and i feel like this book delved deeper in his character development then the trilogy ever did. Newt is the character that really impressed me so much in this book and was the stand out for me in the book of course. <br /><br />WICKED are cunning and very manipulative throughout the whole book and also in the trilogy but what they got these kids to do and endure was so cruel to do. <br /><br /><br /><b>SPOILER WARNING:</b> i recommend you read the Maze Runner trilogy first before reading this prequel because there will be spoilers <br /><br />I loved this book because so many questions were answered and i started to finally remember stuff from when i read the trilogy about 2 and half years ago. </span>

  <span id="freeText991725125089068635" style="display:none"><b>4.8/5</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Our plan is for this to be the command center for what we're calling the Maze Trials, as advance a facility as any research institution has ever had."</blockquote>

<span id="freeTextContainer13908179424818051203">Two years ago, I read the whole <i>Maze Runner trilogy</i> in a month. I'm serious. I bought the three books all together and read them literally non-stop. I clearly liked it but I've never been fully enamoured of it. Then, I read <i>The Kill Order</i>, the first prequel, some months later and I didn't appreciate it as much as I did with the original trilogy. I still think it's the worst in the series and my enthusiasm somehow diminished. Then the films came out and my opinions started to differ. Sometimes I </span>
  <span id="freeText13908179424818051203" style="display:none">Two years ago, I read the whole <i>Maze Runner trilogy</i> in a month. I'm serious. I bought the three books all together and read them literally non-stop. I clearly liked it but I've never been fully enamoured of it. Then, I read <i>The Kill Order</i>, the first prequel, some months later and I didn't appreciate it as much as I did with the original trilogy. I still think it's the worst in the series and my enthusiasm somehow diminished. Then the films came out and my opinions started to differ. Sometimes I preferred the movie (speaking of <i>The Maze Runner</i>) and sometimes I found the book just better (speaking, now, of <i>The Scorch Trials</i>).<br />Then <i>The Fever Code</i> came out and, even if I still don't remember certain things about how the series ended, I HAD to read it. And I'm so glad I did, since now my questions have been answered.<br />It's another prequel and it takes place after <i>The Kill Order</i> and before <i>The Maze Runner</i>. So, we follow Thomas and his friends being taken away from their families by W.I.C.K.E.D. and being trained. They are convinced that they were saved from the Eruption but then Thomas and Teresa become involved in the building of the Maze and they even have to follow from a distance, with the help of hidden cameras, their friends put in there, prived of their memories. Everything was so emotional and creepy at the same time and it's an awful, awful world, the one they live in. Just plain terrible. But it's somehow entertaining, to read about. It seems strange, I know.<br />If you read the trilogy but you have been disappointed like me by the first prequel, don't hesitate but read this one because it gives the answers to a lot of the questions left unsolved in the last instalment of the trilogy, <i>The Death Cure</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13908179424818051203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

You can see their character development so much better! As a result, I still hate Teresa!! Ugh she</span>
  <span id="freeText9572077901893615591" style="display:none">When I started this and found out it was going to be about Thomas and Teresa I was really nervous. I loved The Maze Runner, I thought The Scorch Trials was quite good, but I was so disappointed by The Death Cure ....<br />This was such a turn around from the last book and I am so happy to say it exceeded all my expectations! <br />I enjoyed watching Thomas and Teresa grow up and develop in WICKED headquarters. You can see their character development so much better! As a result, I still hate Teresa!! Ugh she's so awful! <br />It was really cool getting inside information on how WICKED came to be as well. Everything that went on behind the scenes, who knew who before the Maze... all of it was really cool to read about. </span>

<div id="review_1769601752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1769601752" />
    <a title="Clownlab" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51305050-clownlab"><img alt="Clownlab" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1769601752?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clownlab" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clownlab" href="/user/show/51305050-clownlab">Clownlab</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51305050-clownlab?shelf=bookshelf">bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1769601752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1883477826011615570">I started this book with the intention of pacing out my reading of it. Then I started reading it. Three days later, I'm finished. <br/><br/>I started out loving this book. Newt's prologue at the beginning was heartbreaking and emotional: a great way to start. As the book went on, I was happy to see some of the same humor and character personalities that made me love the Maze Runner, Scorch Trials, and Death Cure. <br/><br/>Once I got to the last fourth of the book, I was enjoying it still but rather disappointed th</span>
  <span id="freeText1883477826011615570" style="display:none">I started this book with the intention of pacing out my reading of it. Then I started reading it. Three days later, I'm finished. <br /><br />I started out loving this book. Newt's prologue at the beginning was heartbreaking and emotional: a great way to start. As the book went on, I was happy to see some of the same humor and character personalities that made me love the Maze Runner, Scorch Trials, and Death Cure. <br /><br />Once I got to the last fourth of the book, I was enjoying it still but rather disappointed that there were none of James Dashner's usual ingenious plot twists. I loved the characters and background details so much, that it wasn't a huge deal. It was just pretty disheartening. <br />Then came the epilogue.<br />The epilogue made the book a winner for me: it includes a huge plot twist that labels it a James Dashner masterpiece. It's making me reread the whole series because I want to read those books with the game changer in mind. It's a genius creation.<br /><br />James Dashner has done it again: he's created a master plot, wrote real characters, and made me cry, laugh, smile, and gasp. <br /><br />Now, if anyone needs me, I will be sobbing in a corner clutching my Maze Runner books and rereading them all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1883477826011615570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13113930664609902525" style="display:none">For the love of god don't read this. I know anyone even considering reading this book must be a die hard fan of the series, but please seek immediate help, these books will make you dumber.<br /><br />A SCIENCE FICTION WRITER SHOULD HAVE SOME VAGUE UNDERSTANDING OF SCIENCE.<br /><br />Then again, he's human and he clearly has no idea how normal humans behave, so expecting him to have a grasp of science is expecting way too much.<br /><br />Does he not know how diseases work? Does he not know how the brain works? MAYBE he's going to try to salvage WICKEDs non-sense-science plan in this, but I doubt it, given he made the entire premise of the story worse with his last prequel. <br /><br />I'd put money on him writing the first maze runner book with no idea where he wanted to go with the story, or even a clear understanding of his own world. It's glaringly obvious that, the book is that poorly planed. He just stuck in enticing mysteries and settings just to get readers then stuck in BS explanations as he went on with no really thought or care to it. AVOID!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17031209028919554336"> It's Review TIME!!!!<br/> I am so excited about this review because this book explains SOOOO much about the Maze and what happened before Thomas arrived in the Glade. It also reveals some secrets which I'm don't wanna spoil for you if you haven't read it yet but I just can't help it if one slips out!! For example, NEWT HAS A SISTER!!   <span id="freeText17031209028919554336" style="display:none"> It's Review TIME!!!!<br /> I am so excited about this review because this book explains SOOOO much about the Maze and what happened before Thomas arrived in the Glade. It also reveals some secrets which I'm don't wanna spoil for you if you haven't read it yet but I just can't help it if one slips out!! For example, NEWT HAS A SISTER!! AND SHE'S MENTIONED IN THE WHOLE SERIES!!! AAAAAAAAAAH! I'M FREAKING OUT!!! Not saying who, though! <br /> I enjoyed this book a whole lot more than the Kill Order. I only got a few chapters into the Kill Order and then I stopped because it wasn't very interesting. I will go back and read it sometimes. I checked the Fever Code out from the library and since it was one of the GREATEST books ever, I am definitely going to buy it. I have the whole series except for this one! <br /> I was glad that Dashner included one chapter that was in Newt's perspective but it was very sad :( At least I got a tiny glimpse of his past. I still would like to know more about Thomas and his family though. The only thing I learned about him in this book from his past was his real name. But none of the other Gladers' names were revealed. Except Frypan's, I believe. <br /> Well, here's a summary of my review!<br /> ~ It was AMAZING!<br /> ~ if you loved the Maze Runner series, you MUST buy it!<br /> ~ Secrets are revealed!!!!<br /> ~ Minho is still awesome, sassy, and determined to escape from WICKED<br /> ~ Newt is still my favorite :)<br /> <br />Thanks for taking time out of your day to read my boring (and long) review! :)<br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> <br /> </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711259215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13777977048985123361">So this was the other missing piece to complete the puzzle from the main trilogy of the maze runner.<br/><br/>Fever Code tells the story about the origin of WICKED. The story of Thomas, Teresa, Newt, Minho, Alby, Chuck and more in the WICKED center. How they meet each other before send into the maze. I like the story about little Thomas. He is so cute, smart and ‘special’. They been told that they had been took to that place for good, out from the messy world, the crank and the virus. Although sometimes t</span>
  <span id="freeText13777977048985123361" style="display:none">So this was the other missing piece to complete the puzzle from the main trilogy of the maze runner.<br /><br />Fever Code tells the story about the origin of WICKED. The story of Thomas, Teresa, Newt, Minho, Alby, Chuck and more in the WICKED center. How they meet each other before send into the maze. I like the story about little Thomas. He is so cute, smart and ‘special’. They been told that they had been took to that place for good, out from the messy world, the crank and the virus. Although sometimes they must do a lot of test but they live comfortly in there. They have a room bed, got education, and food. Thomas and Teresa meet one day and be friend. They found that they can do the telepathy and often to use it when communicate. <br /><br />Minho still my favorite from this series. He know there’s something weird happen there, why they had been trapped in that place if that for good. So he ran away but end up with got the punishment. Then it come to the time when their memory been erased and put into the maze. Until this last books Teresa still play the twisted character that will make us confuse rather she is good or bad. <br /><br />So finally it come to an end, I love this book with all the plot and characters. For the last I wanna say that WICKED is bad, I hate for everything that happened to them.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1538383417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7442651777225949588">Eagerly waiting on James Dashner to reply to several tweets confirming that the ending really was what I thought it was. If so, epic twist (in my opinion). Changes SO MUCH about the series. Like, SO MUCH. I can't decide whether to give this book 4.5 stars or 4.9 stars. Maybe depends on whether Dashner replies to me. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z5aPXc1wK3a1OqMSzpO/xv4vc0CorCGPCEj0CXuoDN/rASIv0fqUeFBg7GRLfDDX35DMQr9z7zpf61f67PJjVg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hHVncPkM//JXznGv4tJ0G0Ww+TI5t+VOrJLNvejuvQMI4soC5YZA/LKUPtlnPfsKZA9GMC5oK/v7MW5Of7TSig==')})
  }
